text:
Oh my GAAAAWWWDDDD!  This was the BEST bread EVER!  Here are the changes I made:

* 1 cup of white sugar and 1/2 cup of packed brown sugar

* add 1 tsp. vanilla

* add 1 tsp. cinnamon

* substitute apple sauce for the oil

* cooked in a Pampered Chef mini loaf stone pan (4 small loaves)

* sprinkled Ghiardelli chocolate cooking chips (60% cocoa) on top

* cooked for 57 minutes

* I used 3 overly ripe bananas, which was more than 1 cup

It is so out of this world...chewy on the outside and moist and dense on the inside...but not overly sweet.  I ate a whole mini loaf steaming right of the oven, b/c I couldn't stop.  I'm going to go into a banana bread coma!

Delicioso!

text:
This is wonderful. Yogurt works as well as buttermilk. I also accidentally found out that if you use vanilla yogurt instead of buttermilk, applesauce instead of oil, and cut out the sugar, it's a pretty good low fat, low sugar treat. Better if it sits for a day so the natural sugars can absorb. I've tweaked this recipe a lot and no matter how I make it it's wonderful! Thanks, Rose!

text:
Thanks, Rose, for a wonderful recipe.  I have made this bread several times and it is definitely a favorite.  For a simple topping, mix together 2 TBLS. each finely chopped nuts and granulated sugar with 1/2 tsp. cinnamon and a generous dash of nutmeg.  Sprinkle on batter before baking and press lightly with the back of a spoon.  This topping gives the bread a sweet crunch ~ delicious!!  Thanks, again, for sharing!!!!!!!

This is definitely THE BEST banana bread I've ever come across- but I swear I've made it even better.  Try this-
Take 4 oz. of room temp cream cheese, beat it together with 3T milk until smooth.  Add 1 cup of powdered sugar and 1/2 t. vanilla and mix until incorporated.  Drizzle this over your banana bread when it's done, take a bite and you will swear you've died and gone to heaven.

Wow!  The title of the recipe couldn't be more fitting!  This stuff is the best.  I love banana bread and this one was very moist and oh so good. I used 3 overly ripe bananas that I mashed up so it was a little over 1 cup.  I used 1 cup of white sugar and 1/2 cup of brown.  I added 1 tsp. of vanilla and 1/2 tsp. of cinnamon.  I left out the nuts, but next time I might add in some walnuts. I sprayed my glass pan with Pam for baking (a life saver) and baked it at 350 for a little over an hour.  It smelled incredible and tasted even better - great recipe!

text:
Okay, I've made lots of Banana Bread.  This may satisy the palate of one who is used to eating out and eating processed foods, but if you are a down-to-earth, cook-everything-from-scratch kind of person, this recipe is not for you.  Too sweet, crisp sides (due to the high level of sugar), and not a real banana flavor. It didn't peak and crest, but remained kind of flat (I'm guessing from the lower heating 325 for 1 and 1/2 hour instead of the standard 350 for 1 hour).  It has taught me a lesson though . . .to stick with what works!

This is an exccellent banana bread recipe.  Most recipes I've tried turn out being dry or rather "blah".  I gave this recipe 5 stars (despite some substitutions I made) because of the moistness and great flavor.  I used vanilla yogurt rather than butt4rmilk, 1/2 cup white sugar and 1/2 cup brown sugar, an extra 1/2 cup of mashed banana (I had 4 banans that were beginning to look like a scienc project), an extra 1/4 of flour, and a heaping 1 tsp of cinnamon.  I'm not telling my mom, but this recipe is better than hers.  I will definitely be making banana bread more often now!!

My kids are just getting over some tummy trouble and I wanted to make them a special treat.  I did alter this quite a bit because it's such a good base for banana bread.  I used whole wheat flour instead of all purpose and added about half a can of pumpkin and some spices...cinnamon, nutmeg and allspice.  I also added a big spoonful of sour cream and decreased the sugar to about 3/4 of a cup.  I added a splash of vanilla extract to the egg mixture.  I baked these in miniature muffin tins and got about 48 mini banana muffins. You wouldn't believe how moist these came out. My kiddos would definitely prefer this over a "loaf". Thanks so much Rose.

text:
My husband took one bite of this banana bread and said, "This is the one, don't ever try another recipe."  That was encouraging!  When I took my first bite, it brought back the memories of my mom's recipe, which I have been trying to find for years!  Living in China and not having access to buttermilk, I remembered that my mom would put vinegar into milk for her recipe and wondered if THAT could be the buttermilk.  What WOULD we do without the internet??? YES!  For THIS recipe, add 1 teaspoon of vinegar to 1/3 cup of milk and let it stand for 5 minutes.  Voila!  The buttermilk! (For 1 cup of buttermilk, add 1 Tablespoon vinegar to a cup and fill to the top with milk and let stand for 5 minutes.) Thank you SO much for this wonderful recipe!  It is a huge hit and disappears almost as fast as I can bake it!

text:
Wow this was good!  I've tried multiple banana breads from this site and they all lacked 'something'.  THIS one worked.  Trying to make it healthier I replaced the 1/3 cup buttermilk with vanilla yogurt, the 1/2 cup vegetable oil was replaced with applesauce, I didn't measure the bananas I just used 3.5 (the other .5 went in my belly), and I reduced the sugar to 1.25 cups, oh and I used 1/2 whole wheat flour and 1/2 regular flour and upped the pecans to 1 cups.  Ok wow...guess I changed this recipe a TON lol.  It's very moist and you can NOT tell these are a tad healthier. nom nom nom________________Just for the halibut I made this recipe again using the above changes AND as written and then I had 4 people blind taste test.  ALL of them picked the healthier version as the better tasting one (including myself)....no kidding.  I was shocked :)
Another update:  I used the recipe (subbing the yogurt and applesauce) and instead of bananas I used shredded zucchini.  IT WORKS for zucchini bread too.  I tossed in about a cup of chocolate chips (I do that sometimes with the banana too) and the zucchini bread was fabulous!

text:
This is definately the best banana bread I have ever had. It is moist! I don't use butter milk, because I never have it on hand, regular milk works just fine. I also like to make a little more healthy by using 1/2 whole wheat flour and half white flour. I almost always just add 3 bananas- it is more than 1 cup- but is really yummy. Also I only use 1 cup of sugar.  This time I used brown sugar- if you use the brown, be sure to mix it in with the bananas. If you try to mix it with the flour the sugar stays clumpy- I know because I tried that the first time!  I have made this banana bread many times and it always comes out good, even with all of my tweaking of the recipe.

This recipe is great the way it is, especially if you like sweet banana bread.  I wanted to use less sugar so I cut it down to 3/4 cup and it's still plenty sweet. I am a 'nut' person and used 1-2 cups of walnuts-I don't even chop them, the more the better.  So good, moist and flavorful.  Keeps well too.

I bake for some of the most finicky folk on the planet, one of whom turns up her nose if a baked good contains cinnamon or "too much" vanilla! Another won't eat anything that is "too sweet." Two will not eat nuts. (I know... but they're a pretty good bunch otherwise!)This bread is so moist and flavorful that ALL of them were impressed and have requested it! Once I did not have buttermilk so I used fat-free vanilla yoghurt ( 1 to 1 substitution) and that tasted great too. When I make it for my house I use the pecans and add 1Tbs Penzey's "cake spice" which gives a warmer flavor. In short, this IS the best banana bread recipe I've ever come across in its origional form and with minor alterations made for necessity or personal preference.

text:
A definite 5 stars! The title "Best Ever Banana Bread, fits this recipe to a "T". It is moist and delicious! I had a little over a cup of ripe bananas that I mashed up. I also added a 1/2 cup of chopped pecans to the batter and mixed everything. I sprayed my 9x5 glass pan with Pam, poured the batter in and baked it at 350 for an hour and 5 minutes. The aroma smelled just incredible -filling up my house with a wonderful "banana-y" scent! The bread rose up nicely and produced a nice even brown color. It is moist, flavorful and delicious!  The buttermilk and oil obviously contributes to the moistness of the bread. Not only is this filled with great flavor but it's nicely dense on the inside. The "banana" taste is pronounced in the bread and is not overly sweet! I also like the crunch of the pecans, which is a nice change from the usual walnuts in banana bread.

This truly is THE best ever banana bread, in my opinion. I have tried a ton of recipes over the years, but now that I have found this one, I will never use anything else! I did make a couple of changes. I used half whole wheat flour and replaced the 1 1/2 cups of white flour with 1 cup of brown sugar (they are still plenty sweet!). I'm glad I waited before I reviewed this. Right out of the oven and this just tastes pretty plain, but the next day!! WOW! What a difference and soooooo yummy!

text:
Very, very good!  For 6 small loaves (6"x3") I doubled the recipe using half cup oil/half cup unsweeted applesauce, 4 med sized brown bananas, 2 tsp. vanilla, and 2/3 c. sour cream instead of buttermilk mixed with the eggs. Used only 1 c. white and 1 c. granulated brown sugar instead of 3 c. white. As suggested by another reviewer, I added the topping of sugar, nuts, cinnamon and nutmeg* prior to baking loaves on a cookie sheet at 325 for 45 minutes.  They came out PERFECT!! Store in loose fitting bags, place a saltine cracker or two in each bag to keep bread from getting too moist.  
*for topping: 3 Tbsp sugar, 5 Tbsp finely chopped nuts, 1 tsp cinnamon, 2 generous dashes of nutmeg

Excellent recipe.  I did make a couple of changes that don't alter the base recipe too much.  I used melted butter instead of the oil, reduced the buttermilk to 1/4 cup and replaced 1/2 cup of the white sugar with brown sugar. I also added 1/2tsp of cinnamon to the flour. Wow. This was awesome. I tried it because I didn't have any butter or sour cream in the house and the recipe my family makes uses both of those. I also had some buttermilk I wanted to use up. This banana bread was fantastic when steaming hot and fresh out the oven. I don't even know if I'll be able to review how it tastes after sitting because I am basically shoveling it into my mouth as fast as I can eat it. I added a splash of vanilla extract and cinnamon, and I substituted walnuts for pecans and 1 1/4 cups brown sugar instead of the 1 1/2 cups white because I really like my banana bread moist. I used four really ripe bananas and although it says "mix well," by habit I prefer to limit the amount of stirring I do with my spoonbreads, pancake batter, etc so I only folded the wet ingredients in gently. Stuck it in the oven for 50 minutes in a loaf pan. I am thinking of topping with bananas next time or a brown sugar topping for a bit of a crunch.

text:
This is a great recipe. I usually use an extra half cup of banana. To make this a "lighter" version I subsitutue apple suace for the vegetable oil and it still taste great and cuts out a lot of calories. Also this bread shouold not be served right away. It tastes best the next day. The banana flavor is much more powerful the day after than right before. Although I have a hard time keeping my husband away from the warm bread just out of the oven.

- Side note: I have read some reviews that said the did not use buttermilk. I would not recommend leaving out the buttermilk... in any recipe that calls for it. Buttermilk gives a great flavor and the bread would just not be the same without it.

text:
I made a lot of my own alterations so I'm not even sure this counts, but it came out delicious and the buttermilk idea was a really good one for making the bread supermoist.  Here are the substitutions I made, mostly to reduce the calories -- plain non-fat yogurt instead of buttermilk (works in pretty much all recipes calling for buttermilk, as far as I can tell), used half all purpose flour and half whole wheat flour, only used 1/4 c. or less of oil and about 1/3 c. of cinnamon applesauce, only used 3/4 cup of sugar in total (1/2 c. brown, 1/4 c. white -- it was still plenty sweet, probably in part because of all that cinnamon applesauce), and added about 1 tsp. cinnamon, 1/2 tsp. nutmeg, 1/4 tsp. ginger, and 1/8 tsp. ground cloves to the flour before mixing the dry ingredients with the wet (the spices are just personal preference -- they give it a sort of spicy pumpkin pie flare).  I was in love with a different banana bread recipe from this website, but this one is at least as good even after making all the substitutions to make it healthier.  A very forgiving and tasty recipe!  I recently froze an extra loaf and thawed it a week later.  It tastes even better than the loaf I ate immediately.  This bread definitely freezes well.

Spectacular exactly as written with the exception of the cooking time which is a bit too long.  In my oven 1 hr. 15 min. was perfect, but at 1 hr. 20 min. the bottom was getting a bit too dark.  I don't understand the reviews about 'too sweet'.  It was perfectly balanced in my opinion but also keep in mind that if you use very ripe bananas you could easily cut back on the sugar as very ripe bananas have more sweetness than just plain old ripe bananas.  I also don't understand reviews that make adjustments that don't work out and then give the recipe a lower rating because of it.  eg.  Using too many bananas then giving a 2 star rating!  Come on - if you alter the recipe and it doesn't turn out, don't blame the recipe!

text:
LOVELY banana bread :)
For a VEGAN version, I substituted for the eggs with two flaxseed "eggs", and the milk with almond milk. Couldn't even tell it was vegan. It was gobbled up in no time! For 2 a flaxseed eggs you will need to combine 6 tbls of warm water with 2 tbls of ground flaxseeds. Mix it and let it sit for a about 5 min on the counter, and voila! you have a flaxseed egg substitute. The consistency should be the same slimy consistently as eggs whites. With the almond milk and flaxseed egg you have a banana bread with less cholesterol and less fat, without compromising the taste. Hope that helps. Happy baking everyone.

text:
Delicious.  I was in a kitchen with limited ingredients, so I used vanilla greek yogurt with a touch of milk instead of buttermilk.  I also used approximately half the recommended sugar because I was wasn't in the mood for a sugar bomb. I also sifted in (these are all approximate) 1/2 teaspoon ginger, 1/4 t cloves, some fresh grindings of nutmeg, and 3/4 t cinnamon.  Also some vanilla in the wet mix.  

The crust is amazing. So chewy crispy, straight out of the oven.  We ate half of this loaf standing in the kitchen, armed with a butter knife and our bare hands.  Chicken soup bubbling away on the stove; so naughty! But as my grandfather would say - 'Eat dessert first! They might drop the bomb.'

text:
This is a phenomenal recipe! I never have buttermilk on hand so I usually measure the milk and add a little bit of lemon juice to it. Let it sit about 5 minutes and it's good to go. I also add a little bit of cinnamon, 1 tsp vanilla extract, walnuts instead of pecans and Craisins (dried cranberries). The baking time will vary, but stick a toothpick in the center and when it comes out clean--its done. 

I have made this time and time again and it is ALWAYS a hit. I usually have to make two or three loaves because guests never leave me any!

Next time I will try applesauce instead of oil, just to try something different.

text:
Great resipe! Delicious, moist cake. 
I did alter the recipe some though and it came out amazing: 
I used 1/2 cup light brown sugar, 1/2 cup white sugar and 1/2 cup dark brown sugar.
I replaced the vegetable oil with coconut oil and I replaced the buttermilk with plain yogurt and about 2 tbps of melted butter.
I also cut back on the baking time about 15 minutes.
One of the other reviewerss had a great suggestion for a crunchy top coat, so before popping in oven. I mixed together a tsp sugar with about 2 tbsps cinnamon and a good dash of nutmeg, sifted it together along with crushed walnuts and sprinkled this mixture on the top, pressing it gently down with the back of a spoon. 

It came out very moist in the center with a great sweet crunch on the top. So tasty!

text:
This banana bread is AWESOME!  Because I like extra spice and flavor, I did make a couple modifications per other reviewers' suggestions:  used 1 cup white sugar + 1/2 cup brown and added 2 tsp vanilla, 1-2 tsp cinnamon, a couple dashes of nutmeg, and a large dollop of plain yogurt.  Also, I added the following topping suggested by another reviewer:  mix 2T finely chopped nuts, 2T granulated sugar, 1/2 tsp cinnamon, and dash of nutmeg, sprinkle onto batter, and lightly press with back of a spoon.  The combination of moist bread and crunchy topping is amazing.  I didn't have pecans so I used walnuts in both the bread and topping.  I will be making this again and again..

I had some leftover buttermilk that needed using along with 3 overripe bananas so this is the perfect recipe for that.  I baked at 350degrees for 1 hour and it was perfect...didn't want to hold up the oven for the extra 20 min at 325..I usually bake all my sweet breads at 350 for 50-60 min...that is pretty standard.  Only changes I made was adding vanilla extract and a tsp. of banana extract.  **I could see that this being a thin batter could not take the addition of solids such as nuts or mini chips...they would only sink to the bottom.  I see that other reviewers had trouble with sinking and sticking to bottom of pans and this could be why.  I'll keep this recipe for when I have another surplus of buttermilk

text:
I just realized I may have already reviewed this a long time ago, but I always come back to this recipe as a dependable foundation for my banana bread. Because I often end up with two rotten bananas instead of three, I toss in a bit of greek yogurt or apple sauce to make up the difference. I also add cinnamon, and sometimes a bit of cocoa powder. My tip to people like me who never have buttermilk around the house, is that you probably do! Just pour a little splash of white vinegar into a third cup, and pour some milk on top of it. Let it sit for a minute if you want to see it start mixing.

text:
Look no further, this is an amazing recipe. With a few tweaks it truly becomes the perfect banana bread. As others have suggested, substitute vanilla yogurt (I use Greek) for the buttermilk. Also, use 1/2 cup applesauce + 1T vegetable oil instead of the full 1/2 cup oil. Use 1 cup brown sugar + 1/2 white instead of 1.5 cup white. Add 1/2T each of vanilla and cinnamon. Finally, mix up a little vanilla, milk & confectioner's sugar & pour over loaf immediately after removing from the oven. 
Never before have I felt so compelled to rate/review/share a recipe online. No doubt about it, this is the best!

text:
Makes a perfect loaf of banana bread. I didn't have any buttermilk so I made my own by adding 1 tablespoon of white vinegar to a cup of milk and allowing it to set for 5 min. After the 5 min I measured out the appropriate amount and added it to my mixture.  I followed the suggestions of others and used applesauce in place of the oil.  I also added 1 TB each of cinnamon and vanilla, and used a combination of white and brown sugar. I followed the cooking time to the minute, and it was perfect.
This isn't an overly sweet bread, and I think the substituting in of apple sauce causes it to lose some of its moisture. Next time I'll try half/half apple sauce and oil and maybe add another banana.

I followed another reviewer's suggestion and used 1/2 C of brown sugar and 1 C of white sugar.  But I also added 1 t of cinnamon, and 1 t vanilla.  I think it could have actually done with a little less sugar, but it's a great banana bread.  I was worried about the batter because I've never made a quickbread with such a runny batter.  But it baked up beautifully.  It took about an hour and a half for me - still quite wet in the middle at 1:20.  But it was worth the wait.  Definitely a keeper!  I added pecans and it's the perfect add.  I might reduce the sugar and add a streusel on top next time.

text:
Delish!  I've made several banana bread recipes from this site including the Oatmeal Banana Bread and Banana Banana Bread.  I find this one particularly fluffy and it has the perfect consistency for a bread (not too dense and not too wet).  I have to admit that I made them into muffins because it was late and I couldn't wait the 1 hour and 20 minutes it called for.  I baked them on a muffin pan at 375 degrees for 30 minutes.  It yielded 12 very large muffins.  I also did a crumbly topping that included the pecans (instead of in the batter).  Next time if I am adding the crumbly topping I will probably cut the sugar by 1/3 (1 cup instead of 1.5 cups).  I substituted 1/2 cup of the sugar for brown sugar as other reviewer suggested and added more than 1 cup of bananas (about 1.5 cup) because I needed to use 4 medium bananas I had.  Great recipe!! Thank You :)

text:
I made this over the weekend so my husband would have breakfast for the week, as banana bread isn't my favorite, and because I had a ton of bananas in my freezer to start using up. The bread turned out great, moist, and beautiful! I made a couple of changes, as recommended by others. I didn't have buttermilk so I used vanilla yogurt (Dannon light n fit), I used 4 large over-ripe (thawed from the freezer) bananas. I used 1/2 c. white suger and 1/2 c. brown sugar), a heaping tablespoon of cinnamon and then I coated the pan with cinnamon/sugar and topped with brown sugar/cinnamon. I baked for 1 1/2 hours, as a knife in the center never seemed to come out dry, however after cutting into I discovered a large piece of banana in the center that might have been the culprit. The bread turned out very moist and the sugary topping added that little extra something. I also left out the nuts as I'm not a big fan of banana-nut bread. Will be making this recipe again!

text:
I was asked to use up a big bag of old frozen bananas(the kind that look so unappetizing), and this looked like the way to do it...I don't think I could have found a better recipe!  I took the advice of some others here... doubled the recipe to use my bundt pan.  Cut down the egg just a little, reduced the oil as well and added applesauce to make up for the difference.  I was using super "aged" bananas so halved the sugar, using a mix of white and brown.  The bread was still plenty sweet.  I would use even less sugar next time if using super ripe bananas .  I also took advice of others and used the sugar in the pan for extra fun crust and added a splash of vanilla.  I also added 1/3 cup wheat germ and used half white whole wheat flour.  This IS a very friendly recipe and lets you make a super tasty even healthy treat out of bananas that look terrible!

text:
Three simple words to describe this bread --"OH MY GOSH!"  Couldn't have a better name!  I have tried numerous recipes for banana bread over the years and have never found the "perfect" one.  Now I have!  Made some very simple alterations...  Subbed half the white sugar for brown sugar.  Makes bread a beautiful dark color.  Added just a sprinkle of cinnamon.  Also because I live in a VERY high altitude area I added about a 1/4 cup more flour as I always do to breads, cakes, or cookies!  One more little change..instead of buying buttermilk I used the buttermilk powder I had on hand.  I sifted the powder with the dry ingredients...then added the amount of water needed to the liquid mixture. It worked fine!  Also double the recipe and it worked ok...just make sure you have a pretty heavy duty mixer...cuz it makes a lot!!

text:
This is one of the best recipes that I have come across for banana bread; it makes a very moist and delicious loaf. I did make a couple of minor adjustments. I added a teaspoon of vanilla to the batter, and I also sprinkled the loaf with a cinnamon-sugar mixture. Before removing the bread, I let it sit in the pan for 5 min, and I then let it cool on a rack for 10 min. Once it had cooled for 10 min, I wrapped the loaf in tin foil to allow the cinnamon-sugar mixture to moisten, rather than stay powdery. If you do not have pecans on hand, walnuts make a good substitute. Also, I found that 2 bananas equaled a cup. This recipe can also be used to make muffins, which come out equally as delicious as the loaf.

text:
This recipe is good but not spectacular. There are better recipes on this website (there is one using cream cheese as an ingredient that is the best).  But I had all these ingredients on hand and I had some very ripe bananas so this is the one I chose.  Very moist, good banana flavor without being too banana-y.  I followed the recipe exactly but it might be a tad bit better with a splash of vanilla in the batter. One thing it wasn't is attractive - Mine did not dome at all and so the top was super flat.  I made a double recipe and it made 8 mini loaf pans. I like using the mini loaf pans because I seem to get a more even bake.  With the big pans, the edges and sides seem to get too done while the middle remains doughy.  I brought this bread to work this morning and everyone raved about it.  It is very tasty and also very easy to make.  You can put it all together and get them in the oven in less than 15 minutes.

text:
Ive been trying lots of different recipes for banana bread and this one turned out perfect!  Our favorite so far!  I did make some modifications / substitutions as follows:
Since EVERYTHINGs better with butter, I substituted butter for the oil and creamed the sugar, butter and eggs together with some vanilla extract and a touch of ground cardamom and cinnamon and nutmeg.  I made a double batch but only used the amount of sugar recommended for 1 batch.  Did 1 cup white sugar and a half cup brown sugar.  In addition to the baking soda, I added some baking powder and got an absolutely perfect rise.  After I started the recipe I realized I only had 3 bananas = 1 cup and I needed an additional cup.  I had apple sauce on hand and put in a cup of that. (Next time Ill make sure I have more bananas!).  I also added some chocolate chips along with the chopped pecans.  Lastly, I baked at 350 instead of the recommended 325.  Heavenly!

I understand that ratings should be based on the original recipe, but there is benefit in doing both--recognizing a recipe for its general value but adding additional value in changes that enhance the original recipe.  Thank you Rose for this recipe!  And thank you to all the reviewers who offered additional enhancements!  I baked this with apple sauce instead of oil, and added some cinnamon and replaced a third of the sugar with brown sugar.  All minor changes, and with or without these changes, this is a great recipe.
I'm not sure why the original recipe suggested 1 hour and 20 minutes to cook, but I would say no more than 60 minutes is needed.

So disappointing! I followed this recipe exactly, although I had to make my own buttermilk (1/3 cup milk with 1 tsp. lemon juice...let sit for 5 minutes), which is a standard substitute. For as much sugar as is in this recipe, it was not as sweet and did not have as strong of a banana taste as I would've liked. I added the optional pecans, which I think made the bread seem even more dry. I like pecans, but did not like their flavor in this bread.

I will keep searching for a more moist, stronger banana-flavored bread.

text:
Really this is the perfect Banana Bread. No need to look any further, I promise you.  It's not greasy, it's tastes of bananas, not spices.  It is tender and somewhat dense on the inside with the outside baking up a beautiful golden brown.  Perfect just as it is, no need to mess around with it.  However, this is a great recipe to tweak to your tastes.  You can reduce the sugar to 1 cup without sacrificing sweetness, and I have found I prefer it this way.  Try doing 1/2 brown sugar and 1/2 white sugar; it imparts a darker sweetness that is nice.  You can add vanilla, cinnamon, nutmeg-so many variations for one go to recipe.  Add this one to your recipe box, 'cause it's a keeper!

I've been making this fabulous recipe for years since finding it in a Taste of Home magazine.  Two very minor differences in that published version:  the addition of 1 tsp. of vanilla with wet ingredients, and it calls for 1 C of walnuts instead of 1/2 cup pecans. I wrap the cooled loaf tightly in foil, and we wait until the next day to eat it.  That wait is torture, but it really intensifies the moistness and deep banana taste.  (By the way, for you cooks who like to lick the bowl, this uncooked batter may just become your favorite - it surely is mine.)

text:
I must have tried a dozen different banana bread recipes and this is by far the best, with the deepest, truest banana flavor. (I think recipes that use butter and vanilla somehow interfere with the banana flavor.) The second time I made this, I substituted low fat sour cream for the buttermilk. Plain vanilla yogurt would also work well, or you could add 1 tsp. lemon juice to 1/3 cup milk to create a quick buttermilk. (That's my trick for buttermilk pancakes.) For those who don't want to wait the 80 minutes for this to bake, try using a Bundt pan and turn up the heat to 350 degrees. It took 45-50 minutes, almost half the time, and the only difference was a slighty darker crust. After years of searching, this is now my go-to banana bread recipe.

This was fantastic!  I used this recipet, as I only had one bread pan.  (I will get another and double this recipe).  I had a pt. of fresh blueberries I wanted to use, so added them also.  It took about 10 min. longer to cook, but it came out DELISH!  My grandkids, who are all picky eaters, had 2 slices each and wanted more!  Unfortunately, it was all gone! I never have buttermilk on hand nor do I want to throw out the rest of a huge container of it!

text:
After reading reviews, I made several changes to "healthy up" the recipe.  My rating is for the healthy version.  That being said, with how tasty mine turned out, I am SURE the full-fat, higher sugar version would be AWESOME :D  I changed the following: used 1/3 cup light vanilla yogurt instead of buttermilk, 1/2 cup applesauce instead of oil, used almost 2 cups of bananas, only 1/2 cup of sugar (brown sugar that is- the bananas have enough sugar), and added 1/4 cup extra flour since the extra banana makes it stickier.  I also added 1 tsp cinnamon and 1/4 tsp nutmeg.  The end result had a delicious spicy banana flavor, but the spongier texture you would expect from a bread with no oil.  I did a ballpark calorie count and each slice (12 slices/loaf) ended up having about 170 calories- not bad for banana bread.  I shared it with some friends and they claimed they couldn't tell it was healthy.  I would highly recommend these alterations if you are looking to cut fat and calories!  I'd make this again for sure!

text:
"Best Banana CAKE Ever" -- it's wonderful, but as written: it's flat-out cake.  Cut the sugar a tad (and use at least some brown sugar, no matter what), increase the bananas, substitute half the oil with applesace and about 1/3 of the flour with wheat flour, and you'll have a delightful, moist banana bread.  That's how I usually make this, but I was out of applesauce and forgot to cut back on the sugar until it was too late.  Even with more bananas and the wheat flour, it still tastes like something Little Debbie would make.  Which means it tastes FABULOUS, but I'm only giving it 4 stars, because I don't think the title of the recipe accurately reflects the finished product.

Ridiculously delicious!! I modified this but it came out spectacular so i had to share.  I did not have buttermilk so i used 1/3 c. of sour cream, substituted 1/2 c. of applesauce instead of the veg oil, used three bananas (they were brown and needed a plan fast!!), I used 1 c. of brown sugar instead of 1.5 c. of white, and whole wheat flour instead of white flour (and i did use the pecans). This is really a 4.5 but I made this three times in one day, all a little different. In the best batch I used half splenda and half sugar. I used egg beaters instead of eggs, and smuckers oil substitute intead of vegetable oil. I used 1 tablespoon of sour cream, 3 tablespoons of evaporated milk instead of buttermilk (it's all I had on hand I used all the yogurt I had on the first two batches). I added 1 teaspoon of banana extract/flavor and 1/2 a teaspoon of pure vanilla extract with a light dash of cinnamon. I sugared the bottom as someone else suggested and sprinkled nuts and sugar on top of batter. I took the recommendation from previous reviews to bake 45 min then cover lightly for the next 15.  Mine were all done at 1 hour. They were GREAT!

text:
With the addition of 1 tsp. vanilla this is exactly my mom's "secret?" recipe. :) Funny she had us fooled all those years! 
Her notes were, "bake @325 until top is golden and splits slightly about 1 1/2 hrs but check at 1 hr and watch, do not over cook."
We love that it's a dense bread, not fluffy cake-like. 
So many people ask me to make it! If you like, it's also good later, toasted lightly with a little cream cheese.

text:
This is a great basic banana bread recipe. I experimented a tiny bit.  My eggs on hand were small, so I used 3. I used 3 tbsp buttermilk powder instead of liquid. I used 1 tsp each of baking soda and baking powder. I used 1 c sugar and substituted 1/2 c honey, to total 1.5 c sweetness. 3 small very ripe bananas = 1.25 cups mashed banana. Also added 1 tsp vanilla. I added 3 tbsp chia seeds, hydrated in 1/2 c water for 2 minutes. (Just trying to add some goodness!) Result was fantastic! Oh, and I used my silicone baking pans for the very 1st time. I did not add nuts, but the chia seeds gave it a slight nutty consistency. Baking time was 45 min for 2 small loaves. YUMMY!

text:
Like many of us who love to bake, I'm always on the look out for a bread that is more perfect than the previous one we've deemed a "10"!! 
This bread, by far, is THE best recipe i've ever made..and this coming from someone who is well known to make a mean banana bread! Love the recipe, thank you, Rose!
As for changes, i used half coconut oil and half applesauce and used an equal mix of brown and granulated sugar called for. I also added a tsp of vanilla because i love vanilla in breads. 
Added a topping at the request of my daughter, but this  bread is def stand alone terrific.  
Crumble topping-
1/2 C brown and 1/2 granulated sugar
1/2 flour
1/2 cup finely chopped nuts
1 tsp cinnamon
5 T butter

text:
This was really easy! I read some reviews first and saw that there were issues with it rising nicely. I just used a heaping teaspoon(or approx 1.5) for the baking soda and it rose perfectly! Also I had pretty fresh bananas and I was afraid that there wouldnt be much flavor from them so I added a teaspoon each of cinnamon and vanilla extract. Also since there were comments about it being too sweet I just cut the sugar in half to 3/4 of a cup and it was plenty sweet. I also didnt have buttermilk and so I substituted vanilla yogurt whey for as much as was sitting in the yogurt pot and then added the actual yogurt to make it the right amount up to 1/3 cup.

Truly the most moist and delicious banana bread recipe I have found! This is my go-to banana bread recipe and every time I make it, it is requested at the next function! Can also make into cupcakes/muffins just as easily. I make it vegan, replacing the milk with nut or soy milk and replacing the eggs with ground flax seeds and water - so easy! If you like a little less sweet so more natural banana flavor shines, you can cut sugar down to just 1/2 cup and it still tastes awesome! Enjoy! :)

text:
I doubled this recipe and decided to do something different with 1/2 the batter. I placed wax paper on a sheet roll baking pan, greased it & dusted flour on the paper. It was done within 30 min while my loaf was still baking. I pulled it off of pan, placed a towel on top and rolled it while it was still hot. I let cool for 30 min. I slowly unrolled it, let it breathe then spread a cream cheese caramel topping on it leaving 1 in on sides. Rolled it up easily, dusted it with powered sugar & drizzled caramel topping on top. Easy, fun & turned out great.

This is a great banana bread. I have made it several times, usually in three small loaf pans cooked for 40 minutes or so. It is so moist and freezes beautifully. I always add vanilla, and sometimes cinnamon,  or chocolate chips or walnuts (instead of pecans). I cut the sugar to 1/2 or 3/4 cup and it is still good, though not as sweet tasting when 1/2 cup is used. Also, spelt flour (white or whole grain) subs nicely for wheat. A family favorite!

I encourage you to use the recipe as is, except if you want to add spices to enhance your bread.  Thank you for this recipe.  I will keep using it.

text:
This was really good in many ways and I think buttermilk is really a key to its moistness and light texture.
I made it twice - once substituting gluten free flour because I was making it for my 3rd graders and I have two gluten intolerant children in the class.  The only switch besides the gluten free flour blend (by Bob's Red Mill) was to add a 1/2 tsp of baking powder.  And no nuts for that one because of the nut allergies in my classroom too.  The kids loved it and for a gluten free banana bread it was very moist and light.  But it was soooo sweet, that I decided to make another one for my husband and I.  I used 1/2 white flour and 1/2 whole wheat (because that's all I had) and I put half the amount of sugar recommended, plus a splash of vanilla, a tsp of cinnamon, and the oil that I used was a mild olive oil (again, that's what I had on hand).  Oh, and I added a 1/2 cup of chopped cashews.   It was plenty sweet still but best of all it was moist and light and delicious.  I've made a lot of banana bread in my life, and the buttermilk makes a huge difference!

text:
The banana bread recipe is a good foundation; however I change a few things to make it the best banana bread ever! .  1.) I add more bananas as I never make one batch of this.  I usually do 3 bananas per batch, it leaves it more moist and more flavorful.  2) replace buttermilk with coconut milk - exact same measurement per batch.  3) replace vegetable oil with vanilla yogurt - again with the exact same measurement per batch.  These changes sound weird, I know; however they leave the bread amazingly moist!  I also make this bread into muffins by simply using a muffin tin.  My husband hates bananas, my best friend hates bananas...I have convinced them both to try this bread as it's so delicious and they both love it; in fact they both request it! My husband likes it to take to work for a quick breakfast, my best friend likes it over coffee or chai tea, and my kids love to bring them to school for snack.  The recipe itself is not something that came out incredibly well; however, with a few adjustments, it was incredible!

text:
I've been using this recipe for years and it's a hit every time no matter who I make it for. It sooo moist, full of flavor, and when it's freshly baked (since it's even better when warm) it has this nice little crust on the outside and is super soft on the inside. I tweak it in the following ways: I generously add a few dashes of nutmeg and cinnamon to the dry ingredients and pure vanilla extract to the wet (1tsp). I don't measure out my bananas (the more the merrier) but I probably use roughly a little more than 2 cups. Also, the full amount of white sugar in the recipe is way too sweet so I split what's called for: half white sugar and half brown sugar and I still hold back a little of the white sugar to cut back on some of the sweetness a little more. This recipe is a keeper.

text:
I absolutely loved the recipe! I was hesitant to  amount of sugar it called for, but  then again I dread banana bread that lacks the extra sweet flavor. I did make my own tweaks, and I must say I am impressed with the results! 

Added to the wet ingredients:
1 TSP VANILLA

Added to the dry ingredients:
1 TSP BAKING SODA
1  TSP CINNAMON

I opted for walnut pieces instead of almonds and a muffin tray instead of a loaf pan.

Instead of mixing walnuts in the batter, I just topped the muffins off before the went in the oven. 

For baking time and temperature:
Baked in oven at 425 degrees for 5 minutes,.
Then drop temperature to 350 degrees for an additional 12 minutes.

These Muffins turned out perfect and I cant wait to share them!

Most banana bread is dry and bland...this is completely NOT. Very moist with a great banana flavor. It is dense without being rubbery or gummy. I had three over-ripe bananas but was low on butter, so I looked for an alternate recipe that uses oil rather than my usual butter/sugar recipe. This is good! It looked perfect coming out of the oven and is definitely moist, as others have said. I did reduce sugar by 1/2 cup based on reviews, but next time I might just stick with it as written. It sounded like a lot of sugar at first, but then I saw that my usual recipe calls for 1 cup anyway.  I liked the idea of combining the mashed bananas with the wet ingredients rather than into the batter at the end. Since I almost never have buttermilk on hand and I always have sour cream, I used that instead.

I made this into 4 mini loaves, and I'm glad I checked at 37 min because they were ready. The next time I'd check it sooner.  I used 1 cup white and 1/2 cup brown sugar. I also added 1 tsp cinnamon, 1 tsp vanilla, 2 tblsp ground flax seed, and about 1/4 cup chopped walnuts. My bananas were good-sized and I used three (that equaled just over a cup for me when mashed). Before placing in the oven, I topped with cinnamon-sugar and some Ghiradelli 60% cocoa baking chips. It came out delicious! UPDATE 8/29/19: This time I added a handful of chocolate chips to half of the batter. Also using mini-loaf pans, I sprinkled a few of the chips on top of the two that had them in it.

text:
Liked this one a lot. Followed the recommendation of a few others on some modifications -- used 1 banana; 2/3c applesauce (instead of oil); added 1 tsp of cinnamon; added 1/2 c of raisins; used 1/2c white sugar, 1/2c brown sugar and 1/2 c stevia powder; used 1c AP flour and 3/4c wheat flour. I used lowfat buttermilk (since I had some and am trying to use it up).

All I have is a mini-loaf pan - and this came out to 6 mini loafs. I cooked it at 350 for 25 minutes -- came out great. A little crunch on top, I would say density is medium, while retaining plenty of moisture.

My whole family loves this recipe!  I've already made at least 6 in the past 3 weeks!  Thank you!  I had a tip if you didn't happen to have buttermilk handy:  1 cup milk (skim is ok)with 1 TBSP lemon juice, set aside for 5 minutes and there's your buttermilk substitute!  Still tastes awesome! Okay...this is my first review of a recipe. I made this bread just like the recipes stated and it was soooooo good! Then I made a few changes simply to make it more nutritous and lower calorie. I used applesauce for the oil, vanilla Greek yogurt for the buttermilk, 1/2 brown sugar 1/2 stevia, 1/4 c egg beater and 1real egg, 1/2 whole wheat flour 1/2 all purpose flour. My family loved the healthier version!  I only had two smaller loaf pans so I reduced the temp to 325 and baked them for 50 minutes.....perfect! I added chocolate chips to one loaf. This is a great recipe that you can easily modify to meet your own taste.

text:
EXCELLENT!!!  I made this bread and the "Banana Sour Cream Bread" within a few weeks of each other and this was definitely my favorite of the two.  I doubled the recipe to use up the 5 overripe bananas I had on hand (which yielded just a little more than 2 cups, once mashed)...and actually chose the recipe to use up some buttermilk.  WOW!  It was very moist and had excellent flavor!  It's also worth noting that this bread is very forgiving...my newborn woke up and wanted to nurse towards the end of the baking, so I had to turn off the oven and leave the door cracked as I could not give it my attention at that moment.  I went back to it later and found that it was still very underdone in the center.  I turned the oven back on and baked it for another 20 minutes, all the while thinking the final product would surely suffer, but it came out delicious despite the fragmented baking.

This was an awesome easy recipe. I decided to do a little variation, as follows. I doubled the recipe using plain yogurt in place of the buttermilk. After all of the ingredients are mixed I separated the batter. In one half of the batter I used about a cup of chocolate chips. In the second batter I used 3/4 cup white chocolate chips, 1/2 cup chopped pecans and 8 thinly sliced strawberries. Pour into separate bread pans and viola! two yummy breads :)

text:
I love this banana bread recipe. I've made it many times, sometimes following the recipe exactly and sometimes changing it. Any way I make it, it turns out great. I usually use more bananas than called for (maybe 2.5-3 regular sized bananas) and I use a combination of brown sugar and white sugar. Sometimes I'll add 1 tsp of vanilla and replace the buttermilk with lowfat vanilla yogurt. To make it even healthier, use applesauce instead of oil. I bake it in an 8x8 in glass pan at 325 F for 1 hr. I will keep going back to this recipe whenever I get a banana bread craving.

I was skeptical when I read "Best Ever" recipe.  Who would've thought a basic bread could be made into such a wonderful creation!   I used banana yogurt instead of buttermilk.  I used the oil but will try again with cinnamon flavored applesauce, just to see what happens.   Also used 3/4 c. white and 3/4 c. brown sugar. The only little piece that is left is still moist, 3 days after making this recipe.  One final thought, following the recipe to the letter will yield excellent results but what is also wonderful is that you can tweak it and it will still be "Best Ever".

text:
Oh my goodness, this is the BEST banana bread ever! I will never need to try a new banana bread recipe again! The texture is lovely, the smell heavenly, and the recipe base fun to work with!  I made mine into 22 regular muffins. They came out perfectly at 30 minutes in the 325 degree F oven.  As many have done, I tweaked it. :-)  1) I used 1/4 cup of applesauce and 1/4 cup of oil, instead of the 1/2 cup of oil, to cut back on fat. 2) Instead of measuring out 1 cup of mashed bananas, I just used the four small/medium ones I had. 3) I used 3/4 cup brown and 3/4 cup white sugar. I would think that so much sugar makes it too sweet but it doesn't. It is just right. 4) To add a little fiber, I used 1 cup of white flour and 3/4 cup of whole wheat flour. Next time I might do 1 cup whole wheat and 3/4 cup white. :-) 5) I didn't use the pecans since most members of my family do not like nuts, but I added some pecan bits on top of a few muffins for me. I just put them on, but I would recommend pushing them down a little bit with a back of a spoon so they stay in the muffin and don't pop off when you eat them. 6) I added a splash of vanilla to the egg mixture. 7) I added a heaping 1 teaspoon of cinnamon to the sifted flour mixture. 8) Oh, and last, but not least, I added 3 palm/handfuls (my hands aren't very big)of chocolate chips.  I know it sounds like a lot of changes, but most of them are pretty basic. Thank you so much for this recipe, it's going to go into a special box/folder of f

Had some leftover pumpkin puree and not enough banana mush, so I used about half and half each and it made quite a nice pumpkin bread with a slightly banana-y flavor. As other reviews suggested, I used brown sugar instead of white, cut down on the oil, and added a bit of vanilla extract for more flavor. 

Unfortunately, 1 hour 20 minutes was too long to bake this. Mine could have done with 10-15 minutes less to really be moist and yummy. As it was, it still turned out fine. 

Four stars instead of five because of the over-baking and that I've made much better pumpkin bread from other recipes, although I concede that it's not what this recipe was made for. It was still very good.

This is actually identical to bread I used to make from a Fitness Magazine which I lost years ago.  In the magazine, they'd made healthy substitutions which I mimicked. text:
This banana bread is excellent; true to the title. The loaf is moist, dense, and rich, with excellent banana flavor. I made only one change - I used half brown sugar, half granulated sugar. 
The top of this loaf gets very dark, so be cautious, but don't take it out too early (do the toothpick test) or else the middle will be underdone.
To save this delicious loaf indefinitely, let it cool completely and slice into 1/2 inch slices. Freeze in a large airtight container with slices just apart or separated by wax paper, then you can remove one or a few slices at a time to thaw and eat. The bread also lasts for a long time whole in the fridge, but can pick up some funky fridge flavors if not tightly wrapped.

text:
This is the BEST banana bread recipe EVER! I have tried so many and this one came out perfectly. I was out of vegetable oil, so I used melted butter flavored Crisco shortening, cut the sugar back and used 1/2 white sugar and 1/2 brown sugar, added 1 tsp. of red wine vinegar to the milk and let is stand for 10 mins. as I didn't have any buttermilk, added a teaspoon of vanilla extract and a dash of cinnamon. Baked in three mini loaf pans, greased & sugared, at 325 for 45 minutes. My husband took a loaf to work and I gave one to my neighbor and I've already had several requests for the recipe. This one's a keeper!!!

Wow!  Great banana bread and soooo easy.  I rarely bake as I live at high-altitude and am always worried things won't come out quite right, but this turned out great.  I added about 1/4 cup extra flour to account for living 'a mile high', substituted walnuts for pecans and followed the rest of the recipe exactly.  I also baked it in a pyrex bread dish. It is so moist and flavorful.  Thanks very much for the submission- I am sure my guests this weekend will want to thank you too!
